InVivoStat Repeated Measures Parametric Analysis

Response and covariance structure

The Resp8 response is currently being analysed by the Repeated Measures Parametric Analysis module.

The response has been Square Root transformed prior to analysis.

The repeated measures mixed model analysis is using the compound symmetric covariance structure to model the within-subject correlations. When using this structure you are assuming sphericity and also that the variability of responses is the same at each level of Day 1, see Pinherio and Bates (2002). These assumptions may not hold in practice.

Categorised case profiles plot of the observed data (on the Square Root scale)

Comment: The overall tests in this table are marginal likelihood ratio tests, where the order they appear in the table does not influence the results.

Conclusion: There are no statistically significant overall differences, at the 5% level, between the levels of any of the terms in the table of overall tests.

Tip: While it is a good idea to consider the overall tests in the above table, we should not rely on them when deciding whether or not to make pairwise comparisons.

Diagnostic plot

Residuals vs. predicted plot

Tip: On this plot look to see if the spread of the points increases as the predicted values increase. If so the response may need transforming.

Tip: Any observation with a standardised residual less than -3 or greater than 3 (SD) should be investigated as a possible outlier.

Comment: The standardised residuals are obtained by subtracting the fitted values from the responses and dividing by the estimated within-group standard error.

Warning: As these tests are not adjusted for multiplicity there is a risk of false positive results. Only use the pairwise tests you planned to make a-priori, these are the so called Planned Comparisons, see Snedecor and Cochran (1989). No options are available in this module to make multiple comparison adjustments. If you wish to apply a multiple comparison adjustment to these results then use the p-value adjustment module.

Analysis description

The data were analysed using a 4-way repeated measures mixed model approach, with Treat 1, Treat 2 and Treat3 as treatment factors, Day 1 as the repeated factor and Block1 and Block2 as blocking factors. This was followed by Planned Comparisons on the predicted means to compare the levels of the Selected effect. The response was Square Root transformed prior to analysis to stabilise the variance.

The compound symmetric covariance structure was used to model the within-subject correlations. When using this structure we assumed that the variability of the responses was the same at each level of Day 1 and the correlation between responses from any pair of levels of Day 1 is the same.

A full description of mixed model theory, including information on the R nlme package used by InVivoStat, can be found in Venables and Ripley (2003) and Pinherio and Bates (2002).

For more information on the theoretical approaches that are implemented within this module, see Bate and Clark (2014).

Analysis options

Response variable: Resp8

Response transformation: Square Root

Treatment factors: Treat 1,Treat 2,Treat3

Repeated factor: Day 1

Subject factor: Animal1

Blocking factor(s) selected: Block1,Block2

Covariance structure fitted: Compound Symmetric

Output tests of overall effects table (Y/N): Y

Output predicted vs. residual plot (Y/N): Y

Output normal probability plot (Y/N): N

Show Least Square predicted means (Y/N): Y

Selected effect (for pairwise mean comparisons): Treat 1*Treat 2*Treat3*Day 1

Post-hoc tests: All pairwise comparisons

Significance level: 0.05
